[0:0:66,13] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — GG   196   GENERAL GOVERNMENT 

[1:0:164,43] 9800   Augmentation for Employee Compensation 

[2:0:66,64] This item reflects funding augmentations for state employee compensation. If the Legislature previously appropriated money, 

[2:1:66,74] through this budget item, to pay for the economic terms of employee compensation in previous fiscal years, the funding for 

[2:2:66,84] those economic terms is included in departments' budgets. When economic terms require funding not yet appropriated by the 

[2:3:66,95] Legislature, those funds are included in this budget item. 

[3:0:66,112] Additionally, this item sets aside funding for penalties the state may face under the Affordable Care Act (ACA). Beginning in 

[3:1:66,123] 2015, the state became subject to the Employer Shared Responsibility provision of the ACA. This provision requires large 

[3:2:66,133] employers to offer health benefits to full-time employees, defined as those who work on average 130 or more hours per month 

[3:3:66,143] (or 30 hours per week), and their dependent children. Under this provision, the state may be subject to penalties (Part B 

[3:4:66,153] Penalty), which may include part-time, temporary, and seasonal employees that may have been considered full-time for one or 

[3:5:66,163] more months, were not offered or did not qualify for health benefits through the state, purchased health coverage from the 

[3:6:66,174] Health Insurance Marketplace (known as Covered California), and received a premium tax credit or cost sharing reduction. 

[3:7:66,191] The ACA also contains reporting requirements, which require the state to track specified ACA-related employee information on 

[3:8:66,201] a monthly basis to identify the employees who meet health eligibility requirements, document whether benefits were offered, 

[3:9:66,212] and whether the employee accepted benefits. This data collection is used to report the state's level of ACA compliance to the 

[3:10:66,222] Internal Revenue Service on an annual basis. The state may be assessed penalties for inaccurate reporting (Internal Revenue 

[3:11:66,232] Code sections 6721 and 6722).

[0:0:66,13] GENERAL GOVERNMENT   2018-19 STATE BUDGET — GG   199 

[1:0:207,43] 9818   Federal Levy of State Funds 

[1:1:66,64] The federal courts periodically issue judgments or "writs of execution" against the State of California requiring the state to make 

[1:2:66,74] payments to the federal government. The writs and judgments provide the authority to the federal government to withdraw 

[1:3:66,84] funds from the state bank accounts maintained by the State Treasurer's Office at the various state depository banks. 

[1:4:66,105] Each year, the Budget Act authorizes the Department of Finance to identify specific appropriations or funds to charge when the 

[1:5:66,115] federal government withdraws funds from state bank accounts. When no specific appropriation or fund can be identified, the 

[1:6:66,125] withdrawals are charged to the unappropriated General Fund balance. 

[2:0:66,146] No levies were paid during the 2016-17 fiscal year and none have been paid through June 15, 2018. 

[2:1:66,172] LEGAL CITATIONS AND AUTHORITY 

[2:2:66,191] DEPARTMENT AUTHORITY 

[2:3:66,208] Annual Budget Act, Control Section 9.30.

[1:3:66,84] appropriations, one for each fund type - General, special, and non-governmental cost funds. These appropriations are allocated 

[1:4:66,95] to other departments by the Department of Finance based upon the determination of need.

[1:0:159,43] 9860   Capital Outlay Planning and Studies Funding 

[1:1:66,64] The Governor's Budget (Budget) appropriates funding to be allocated by the Department of Finance to state agencies to 

[1:2:66,74] develop design and cost information for new projects. 

[2:0:66,101] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW 

[3:0:66,119] The Budget appropriates funding to be allocated by the Department of Finance to state agencies to develop more refined 

[3:1:66,129] scope, cost, and schedule information for new projects to ensure estimated project costs are more accurate, funding levels are 

[3:2:66,140] appropriate, and the project scope is feasible. 

[4:0:66,180] SUMMARY OF PROJECTS 

[5:0:198,202] State Building Program 

[5:1:217,207] Expenditures   2016-17*   2017-18*   2018-19*

[0:0:66,13] 2018-19 STATE BUDGET — GG   206   GENERAL GOVERNMENT 

[1:0:168,43] 9885   Reserve for Liquidation of Encumbrances 

[2:0:66,64] For individual department budgets, encumbrances (commitments for the procurement of goods or services which have not yet 

[2:1:66,74] been received by the state) are accrued as expenditures by departments at year-end and included in the expenditure totals. 

[2:2:66,84] This treatment is in accordance with the budgetary/legal basis of accounting and consistent with individual department budgets. 

[2:3:66,102] For the purpose of determining the overall General Fund balance, Government Code Section 13307 requires that 

[3:0:66,112] encumbrances should not be counted as a budgetary expenditure until the delivery of the goods and services. Furthermore, 

[3:1:66,123] Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (GAAP) require that encumbrances be reflected as a reserve against the General 

[3:2:66,133] Fund balance and not as an expenditure, as in budgetary/legal basis accounting. Government Code Section 13306 and state 

[3:3:66,143] policy require compliance with GAAP whenever it is in the best interest of the state. This budget reflects a statewide adjustment 

[3:4:66,153] to reduce expenditures on a budgetary/legal basis by the encumbrance amounts to comply with Government Code Section 

[3:5:66,163] 13307 and GAAP. A reserve of fund balance for encumbrances for this same amount is shown in Summary Schedule 1 for the 

[3:6:66,174] General Fund. 

[4:0:66,191] COMPUTATION OF ENCUMBRANCE ADJUSTMENT 

[5:0:66,209] The State Controller's Office accumulated a preliminary estimated General Fund encumbrance total of $1,164,703,000 from 

[5:1:66,219] 2016-17 year-end financial statements submitted by state departments. For budgeting purposes, encumbrances are estimated 

[5:2:66,229] to be at the same level for the 2017-18 and 2018-19 fiscal years and are assumed to be liquidated (paid) within the next fiscal 

[5:3:66,240] year. The Encumbrance Adjustment Table summarizes the methodology and the calculation for the encumbrance adjustment.

[0:0:66,13] GENERAL GOVERNMENT   2018-19 STATE BUDGET — GG   209 

[1:0:122,43] 9900   Statewide General Administrative Expenditures (Pro Rata) 

[2:0:66,64] Central service agencies, such as Department of Finance, the State Treasurer, the State Controller, and Legislature, provide 

[3:0:66,74] budgeting, banking, accounting, auditing, payroll, and other services to all state departments. The Pro Rata process apportions 

[3:1:66,84] the costs of providing central administrative services to all state departments and funding sources that benefit from the 

[4:0:66,95] services. Amounts apportioned to special funds for their fair share of central administrative services costs are transferred from 

[4:1:66,105] the special funds to the General Fund and the Central Service Cost Recovery Fund. 

[5:0:66,123] Prior to 2016-17, Pro Rata charges to special funds were normally included in the appropriate departmental budgets. This 

[5:1:66,133] budget item included Pro Rata costs directly charged to special funds for those cases where appropriate funding was not 

[6:0:66,143] provided for in departmental budgets. Effective 2016-17, this budget item includes Pro Rata costs charged directly at the fund 

[6:1:66,153] level, rather than each individual appropriation, pursuant to Government Code section 11274.
